    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer5614174915754699236">This is the exquisitely tender story of love that beats desperately against the taboos of Oriental tradition. With great sensitivity, Gibran describes his passion as a youth for Selma Karamy, the girl of Beirut who first unfolded to him the secrets of love. But it is a love that is doomed by a social convention which forces Selma into marriage with another man. Portraying </span>
  <span id="freeText5614174915754699236" style="display:none">This is the exquisitely tender story of love that beats desperately against the taboos of Oriental tradition. With great sensitivity, Gibran describes his passion as a youth for Selma Karamy, the girl of Beirut who first unfolded to him the secrets of love. But it is a love that is doomed by a social convention which forces Selma into marriage with another man. Portraying the happiness and infinite sorrow of his relationship with Selma, Gibran at the same time probes the spiritual meaning of human existence with profound compassion. **Lightning Print On Demand Title</span>

<div id="review_50372790" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50372790" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50372790?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50372790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1749587707806440600">الأجنحة المتكسرة = The Broken Wings, Kahlil Gibran <br/><br/>The Broken Wings is a poetic novel written by Khalil Gibran and first published in Arabic in 1912. <br/><br/>It is a tale of tragic love, set in turn-of-the-century Beirut. A young woman, Selma Karamy is betrothed to a prominent religious man's nephew. <br/><br/>The protagonist, a young man, perhaps even Gibran himself, falls in love with this woman. They begin to meet in secret, however they are discovered, and Selma is forbidden to leave her house, breaking their</span>
  <span id="freeText1749587707806440600" style="display:none">الأجنحة المتكسرة = The Broken Wings, Kahlil Gibran <br /><br />The Broken Wings is a poetic novel written by Khalil Gibran and first published in Arabic in 1912. <br /><br />It is a tale of tragic love, set in turn-of-the-century Beirut. A young woman, Selma Karamy is betrothed to a prominent religious man's nephew. <br /><br />The protagonist, a young man, perhaps even Gibran himself, falls in love with this woman. They begin to meet in secret, however they are discovered, and Selma is forbidden to leave her house, breaking their hopes and hearts.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه نوامیر سال 2006 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: بالهای شکسته ؛ نویسنده: جبران خلیل جبران؛ مترجم: مهدی مقصودی؛ تهران، نشر گل آفتاب؛ 1376؛ در 88 ص؛ چاپ دوم 1377؛ شابک 9649120823؛ در 126ص؛ چاپ دیگر 1384؛ در 160ص؛ همان شابک؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان عرب - سده 20م<br /><br />مترجم: لاله صفدرخان؛ تهران، شیوه، 1380؛ در 111ص؛ شابک ایکس - 964721412؛ <br /><br />مترجم: رضا ابوترابی؛ مشهد، آیین تربیت، سنبله، 1384؛ در 120ص؛ شابک ایکس - 964721412؛ <br /><br />مترجم: لفته مولایی؛ تهران، سپر ادب، 1384؛ در 128ص؛ شابک: 9649627839؛ <br /><br />مترجم: بهروز حسن نژاد؛ تهران، معرفت، 1384؛ در 194ص؛ شابک 9649627839؛ <br /><br />مترجم: جعفر ابطحی، در 106ص؛<br /><br />مترجم: حورزاد صالحی؛ تهران، پل، 1384؛ در 191ص؛ شابک ایکس - 964693563؛ <br /><br />مترجم: حیدر شجاعی؛ تهران، دادار، 1384؛ در 88ص؛ چاپ دوم 1384؛ شابک 9648097186؛ چاپ چهارم 1386؛ پنجم 1387؛ چاپ پنجم 1387؛ <br /><br />مترجم: محمد ابراهیمی کاوری با همکاری لفته مولایی؛ تهران، نیک فرجام، 1385؛ در 127ص؛ شابک 9649627766؛ چاپ ششم 1387؛ چاپ دیگر تهران، آسو، 1394؛ در 132ص؛ شابک 9786007228531؛ در 132ص؛<br /><br />مترجم: محمد ریحانی، هانی ورده؛ قم، امام عصر(عج)، 1388؛ در 159ص؛ شابک 9786005323078؛ <br /><br />مترجم: شهریار وقفی پور؛ تهران، مروارید، 1388؛ در 121ص؛ شابک 9789648838756؛<br /><br />مترجم: شهرزاد بیات موحد؛ تهران، ماهی، 1393؛ در 96ص؛ شابک 9789649971414؛ <br /><br />مترجم: مرضیه صادقی زاده؛ تهران، آلوس، 1394؛ در 132ص؛ شابک: 9786008129417؛ <br /><br />مترجم: جعفر نوعخواه؛ اردبیل، هفت گنج، 1394؛ در 148ص؛ شابک: 9786009601455؛ <br /><br />مترجم: مصطفی طباطبائی؛ تهران، ؟، ؟؛ در 192ص؛<br /><br />چکیده ای از متن: هجده ساله بودم، که عشق چشمانم را با اشعه سحرآمیز خود، باز کرد، و با انگشتان آتشین خود، برای نخستین بار جانم را لمس نمود، و سلمی کرامه، نخستین زنی بود، که با کارهای نیک و زیبای خود، روحم را بیدار نمود، و آنجا که روزها، همچون رویاها، سپری میشوند، و شبها همچون شبهای عروسی، میگذرند، پیشاپیشم به سوی بهشت عواطف علوی، حرکت کرد؛ سلمی کرامه، همان کسی ست، که با زیبایی خود، پرستش زیبایی را، به من آموخت، و با مهربانی خویش، عشق پنهان را به من یاد داد؛ او کسی ست، که نخستین بیت، از قصیده ی زندگی معنوی را، در گوشم نواخت....؛<br /> ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_670219680" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/670219680" />
    <a title="Ahmad Bozorgmehr" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8403066-ahmad-bozorgmehr"><img alt="Ahmad Bozorgmehr" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513475260p2/8403066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/670219680?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Bozorgmehr" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Bozorgmehr" href="/user/show/8403066-ahmad-bozorgmehr">Ahmad Bozorgmehr</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8403066-ahmad-bozorgmehr?shelf=never-to-read">never-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8403066-ahmad-bozorgmehr?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer670219680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11057460544526755674">I haven't read many awful books but for sure this is one of them. I regret not being able to give this book zero or minus something stars. The thing that bothered me the most was the story's apparent agenda: an abhorrent claim to be presenting a perfect love story. The book pretends to be highly qualified by the incessant use of a poetic style including a gazillion metaphors, similes, and borrowing from Bible and classic literature (To tell you the truth all those in this context seemed really r</span>
  <span id="freeText11057460544526755674" style="display:none">I haven't read many awful books but for sure this is one of them. I regret not being able to give this book zero or minus something stars. The thing that bothered me the most was the story's apparent agenda: an abhorrent claim to be presenting a perfect love story. The book pretends to be highly qualified by the incessant use of a poetic style including a gazillion metaphors, similes, and borrowing from Bible and classic literature (To tell you the truth all those in this context seemed really ridiculous to me) while actually turning out to be quite stupid and inept by using all those beautiful images at the service of a highly comic love story. For the starters the plot is stupid: A love at first sight story played by the depressed masochistic dude who has partially no agency (It's the girl who starts the whole thing) and a submissive and again masochistic girl (Funny enough we are told she is intelligent) who is unable of any action. But the funniest character is the daughter's dad. He is very wealthy and in fact a very good guy but he has a small flaw in his character: he sees no fault in marrying his daughter to a guy she doesn't love. The Bishop guy is purely evil and acts as a member of mafia like he sends one of his guys with an order for the old guy: Marry your daughter to my dear relative or else!( I guessed all this from the old guy's dejected face!)And the ambition behind the godfather's action is money! As if he already doesn't have money and the only way to get it is through a marriage! (as we all know the circulation of money happens between two affluent families) The relative guy is a non-person. Actually he doesn't seem to be present there at all! Well I think Gibran thought one bad guy is enough for his perfect story. A question haunted me while I was reading the book: Why didn't Gibran write a piece of poetry or a short short story to save the reader the pain of reading a shallow portrayal of love? When I was done with the book I read what was written on the back of it: "Khalil Gibran, the revered author of The Prophet and The Voice of the Master, reveals [this word shocked me]the poignant secrets and sorrows of first love in this mystical [I would say stupid] masterpiece." The thing is that to me it was more of a master"piss" in love and its complexities. The characters are all stupid in one way or another. The narrator seems mostly like a hallucinated lonely guy who has nothing to do but to imagine things (does he do anything else?!) He tells and tells and tells. He explains things to the reader. In fact it seemed to me that this is Gibran expressing his partial hatred of tradition,Oriental beliefs, male society,and treatment of women (he is again repeating the same objectifying of women but well in a covert way) as if this is his manifesto.In sum, Gibran's book comes up very short even as a mediocre love story. <br />I like some of gibran's quotes as I find them witty and nice. While reading this book I couldn't stop thinking, "this is a really extended one!"</span>
  <a data-text-id="11057460544526755674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2196322855436351893" style="display:none"><u>Rating:</u> <b>
  <i>3,75 stars.</i>
</b><br /><br />This was ROMANTIC AF! I can't find any other word for it. Imagine every dramantic YA fantasy female MC ever and get her to write her love story: It would be this book. BUT this had really good writing. Like awesome writing. With some feminism here and there. Your usual life questions. Aaaand a massive asshole. With a tragic love story thanks to that asshole.<br /><br />As a conclusion: <br /><br />If you can read in Arabic. And you like tragic love stories. And you want some high-quality writing in your life. And you're falling behind on you Gr's reading challenge. Congrats, this book is for you!<br /><br />If you know how serious this book was you will think of my review as a joke.<br /><br />Low-self esteem: It already is a joke. *with a British accent*<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Thanks for reading this and I hope you get a pet.</b>

<span id="freeTextContainer1571303227801676989">A very emotional novel by an amazing author. It recounts the tale of two soulmates who were broken apart by destiny. Two souls who endured and suffered love and sadness. Two spirits who were destined to be apart until death took its part.</span>

<div id="review_179719600" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179719600" />
    <a title="Hasan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5694494-hasan"><img alt="Hasan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548890753p2/5694494.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179719600?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hasan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hasan" href="/user/show/5694494-hasan">Hasan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5694494-hasan?shelf=khalil-gibran">khalil-gibran</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179719600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17906177834700168809">“Ay that tomb grows Gibran's sorrow together with the cypress trees, and above the tomb his spirit flickers every night commemorating Selma, joining the branches of the trees in sorrowful wailing, mourning and lamenting the going of Selma, who, yesterday was a beautiful tune on the lips of life and today is a silent secret in the bosom of the earth.”<br/><br/>The Broken Wings written by Gibran in 1912 is a poetic novel. It is filled with friendship, love, power struggle and pain and suffering that comes a</span>
  <span id="freeText17906177834700168809" style="display:none">“Ay that tomb grows Gibran's sorrow together with the cypress trees, and above the tomb his spirit flickers every night commemorating Selma, joining the branches of the trees in sorrowful wailing, mourning and lamenting the going of Selma, who, yesterday was a beautiful tune on the lips of life and today is a silent secret in the bosom of the earth.”<br /><br />The Broken Wings written by Gibran in 1912 is a poetic novel. It is filled with friendship, love, power struggle and pain and suffering that comes along with any human relationship. I consider it to be a very personal book by Gibran. Much like his “Spirit Rebellious” which was banned and burned in public in Lebanon. The reader will find in this book Gibran’s strict stance on oppression carried out under the hand or in the name of Religion. Gibran in no sense is against religion but he hates those who use religion as a tool to fulfill their personal desires. In this book many issues are highlighted. Such as social issues of the time in the Eastern Mediterranean, including religious corruption, the rights of women (and lack thereof), and the weighing up of wealth and happiness. Gibran used one of his own true life experiences in this book. Detailing his first love and how he lost his beloved Salma to the cruel doctrines of our society. The fact that it is from a true experience of the author makes it all the more haunting and beautiful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17906177834700168809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2865941314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8851151581372657693"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/291.The_Broken_Wings' title='The Broken Wings by Kahlil Gibran' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Broken Wings</a> is a poetic novel written by Khalil Gibran. This novel follows the tragic love story of an eighteen years old boy(Gibran himself) who falls in love with Selma Karamy a beautiful, nobel girl in her twenties from the very first sight. Selma awakened Gibran’s soul to the feelings of love and passion by her purity and grace and her manners. Since the moment they met, both of them shared an inexplicable magnetic spiritual connection towards each other. But unfortunately, this love wa</span>
  <span id="freeText8851151581372657693" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/291.The_Broken_Wings" title="The Broken Wings by Kahlil Gibran" rel="nofollow noopener">The Broken Wings</a> is a poetic novel written by Khalil Gibran. This novel follows the tragic love story of an eighteen years old boy(Gibran himself) who falls in love with Selma Karamy a beautiful, nobel girl in her twenties from the very first sight. Selma awakened Gibran’s soul to the feelings of love and passion by her purity and grace and her manners. Since the moment they met, both of them shared an inexplicable magnetic spiritual connection towards each other. But unfortunately, this love was doomed by society’s strict and thorny conventions and norms that forced Selma into marrying another man.<br />Through his modernist writing style, Gibran can transcend the reader into the realms of beauty, nature and love. His descriptions were so vivid and the imagery he used so astonishing which added a certain depth to his work and deepened the understanding of his words. Gibran also pointed out the hypocrisy of social heads and false social values and the nature of spiritual love above all which caused him some trouble at the time of publishing this book.<br />The only negative aspect of this book is the excessive use of metaphors and similes and the lack of suspense because from the start the reader can predict the outcome of the story.<br />Long story short this is a must-read book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8851151581372657693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12901149950688466117" style="display:none">A poetic Love book. This is Devine.<br /><br />Love is the only freedom in the world because it is so elevates the spirit that the laws of humanity and the phenomena of nature do not alter its course. <br /><br />Khalil Gibran was 18 years old when he fell in love with a beautiful woman named Selma. He was introduced to her by her father Farris Effandi who was an old friend to his Father .<br />Selma lost her father when she was an infant and her father was the richest man in the country, he loved Selma more than anything else in this world.<br /><br />But the Bishop of the country played his wicked plan. The Bishop had a nephew and he wanted him to marry Selma so that the Bishop could acquire Farris Effandi's wealth. <br /><br />But one fine day as of the holy spirits Selma and Gibran fell in love with each other knowing that their destiny was not meant to be together.. <br /><br />Months passed and as per Bishops evil plan , Selma got married to his nephew , Although her Father didn't wish her to marry Bishop's nephew...<br /><br />After few months of marriage her Father died due to illness and Gibran became her only person to her sorrow..<br /><br />Gibran and Selma met each other once in a month. In a temple where they shared their love, sorrow and misery..<br /><br />The Bishop came to know about this .. and Selma worried that her love will be in trouble.. So they ended their Meeting.<br /><br />Five years passed and her husband was treating her like a slave ... she wasn't able to bare a fruit from her...<br />But one day by God's grace she gave birth to a boy at dawn... but God had other plans the boy was born in the dawn and died in the sunrise... she was in great pain she embraced her son and hit herself against the wall.. By the end of the day there were two bodies lying on the ground.<br /><br />She was buried embracing her son and upon her Father's ditch. <br /><br />Simply innocent beautiful love story.🙂<br /><br />Metaphors are so Devine in this book... Beautiful comparison between the feelings and Nature.<br /><br />It is the most beautiful moment were people fell in love and they know they are in love but they don't confront each other they just gaze at each other in Silence.<br /><br />It is said that " That love is Delightful were the destiny isn't meant to be together "...<br /><br />The cup doesn't entice our lips unless the wines color is seen through the transparent crystal❤</span>

  <span id="freeText10738241750241778367" style="display:none">The Prophet was like the gospel of love to me, tenderly selected words making up sentences and igniting your heart with love, joy, emotion, and realization.   <b>The Broken Wings</b>
</i> is another simple yet profound love story depicting the love between a boy and a girl. A simple love story becomes a sacred love song only because of the mastery of Gibran's hand. Kahlil Gibran, the magician. <br /><br />Selma Says, <i>
  <b>Love kills my desires so that you may live freely and virtuously. Limited love asks for possession of the beloved, but the unlimited asks only for itself.</b>

While I really liked The Prophet, this one was unbelievably mediocre. <br/><br/>A tragic love story commingled with contemplations on love, life and grief, while sounds alluring, fell flat on its face, leaving me absolutely cold to the ultra dramatic trials and tribulations of Selma and Gibran; although there were some passages, certain tid-bits here and there </span>
  <span id="freeText6211450078015982782" style="display:none">Kahlil Gibran is kind of a hit or miss writer, his impact on an individual depends on how privy and inclined they are to his spiritual hyperboles. While I really liked The Prophet, this one was unbelievably mediocre. <br /><br />A tragic love story commingled with contemplations on love, life and grief, while sounds alluring, fell flat on its face, leaving me absolutely cold to the ultra dramatic trials and tribulations of Selma and Gibran; although there were some passages, certain tid-bits here and there worth munching over. <br />But ultimately, his overuse of bejewelled metaphors, exaggerated, and ostentatious dialogues rendered whatever little positive impact the book could've had, absolutely nil.</span>

This shows he was well ahead of his time!</span>

<div id="review_1721687103" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1721687103" />
    <a title="Sidharth Vardhan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58296635-sidharth-vardhan"><img alt="Sidharth Vardhan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595750367p2/58296635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1721687103?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sidharth Vardhan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sidharth Vardhan" href="/user/show/58296635-sidharth-vardhan">Sidharth Vardhan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58296635-sidharth-vardhan?shelf=2-asia">2-asia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1721687103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14969619566569610212"><blockquote>
  <i> "Then she looked at me as if she regretted what she had said and tried to take awaay those words from my ears by magic of her eyes."<br/><br/>"I want you to love me as a poet love his sorrowful thoughts. I want you to remember me as a traveller remembers a calm pool in whihc his image is reflected as he drank its water. I want you to remember me as a mother rememebers her child that died before he saw the light,and I want you to remember me as merciful king remembers a prisoner who died before his par</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14969619566569610212" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i> "Then she looked at me as if she regretted what she had said and tried to take awaay those words from my ears by magic of her eyes."<br /><br />"I want you to love me as a poet love his sorrowful thoughts. I want you to remember me as a traveller remembers a calm pool in whihc his image is reflected as he drank its water. I want you to remember me as a mother rememebers her child that died before he saw the light,and I want you to remember me as merciful king remembers a prisoner who died before his pardon reached him."<br /></i>
</blockquote><br />At its roots, it is a story of unrequited love - realistic and so, simple and small. There are some takes on hyprocrisy or religious people:<br /><blockquote>
  <br />
  <i>"Spirtual disease is inherited from one generation to another until it has become a part of the peopl, who look upon it, not as a disease but as a natural gift, showered by God upon Adam."</i>
  <br />
</blockquote><br />...and position of women: <br /><blockquote>
  <br />
  <i>"Modern civilisation has made women a little wiser, but it has increased her suffering because of man's covtousness."</i>
  <br />
</blockquote><br />The prose is poetic - at times, a little malodramatic. It is phrases and images like <i>'falling drops of dew from the eyes of dawn on the leaves of witherig rose'</i> that I love so much. The poet has phrased dialogues into his poetic language, so if you try imagining the scenes in your mind, characters will seem hillarious saying those things.<br /><blockquote>
  <i><br />"A young man's tear is like a drop of dew on the leaf of a rose, while that of an old man is like a yellow leaf which falls with the wind at the approach of winter."<br /><br />"Limited love asks for the possesion of the beloved, but unlimited love asks only for itself."<br /><br />"One thought that will come to you at night will elevate you to glory or lead you to asylum. One look from a woman's eye makes you the happiest man in the world."<br /><br />"Selma, who yesterday, was a beautiful tune on the lips of life and today is a silent secret in the bossom of the earth."<br /></i>
</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14969619566569610212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1928574757" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1928574757" />
    <a title="Anima" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59510944-anima"><img alt="Anima" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604460535p2/59510944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1928574757?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anima" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anima" href="/user/show/59510944-anima">Anima</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1928574757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16352047645338768291">‘The beauty of Selma’s face was not classic; it was like a dream of revelation which cannot be measured or bound or copied by the brush of a painter, or the chisel of a sculptor. Selma’s beauty was not in her golden hair, but in the virtue and purity which surrounded it; not in her large eyes, but in the light which emanated from them; not in her red lips, but in the sweetness of her words; not in her ivory neck, but in its slight bow to the front. Nor was it in her perfect figure, but in the no</span>
  <span id="freeText16352047645338768291" style="display:none">‘The beauty of Selma’s face was not classic; it was like a dream of revelation which cannot be measured or bound or copied by the brush of a painter, or the chisel of a sculptor. Selma’s beauty was not in her golden hair, but in the virtue and purity which surrounded it; not in her large eyes, but in the light which emanated from them; not in her red lips, but in the sweetness of her words; not in her ivory neck, but in its slight bow to the front. Nor was it in her perfect figure, but in the nobility of her spirit, burning like a white torch between earth and sky. Her beauty was like a gift of poetry. But poets are unhappy people, for, no matter how high their spirits reach, they will still be enclosed in an envelope of tears.’<br /><br />"....Will you hear the whispering of my wings in the silence of night? Will you hear my spirit fluttering over you? Will you listen to my sigh? Will you see my shadow approach with the shadow of dusk and disappear with the flush of dawn?..."<br />"The true light that showed me the beauty and wonder of the universe was converted to a great flame of fire that seared my heart; and the Eternal music I used to hear became a clamour, more frightening than the roar of a lion."</span>
  <a data-text-id="16352047645338768291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13692104377410650224">I read this in translation, in English and in Urdu, in fact, in three different Urdu translations, and I was struck by the lightning prose of Gibran. The dream-like, melancholic pining of the protagonist for his beautiful lover takes you to a realm of fantasy that is equally grounded in brutal reality of everyday life. It has been a long time I read it and now that I recall it after over a decade and a half, I am feeling nostalgic.</span>

<div id="review_2953763630" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2953763630" />
    <a title="Muhammad Murad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16272928-muhammad-murad"><img alt="Muhammad Murad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479041143p2/16272928.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2953763630?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Muhammad Murad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Muhammad Murad" href="/user/show/16272928-muhammad-murad">Muhammad Murad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2953763630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer327624521734588643">For me, it's more than just a love story. <br/><br/>It is the story of a father who was compelled to marry off his daughter to the Bishop's nephew because his (Farris Effendi) and his daughter - Selma Karamy's reputation would have been ruined had he said no to Bishop. As mentioned in the book, "No man could disobey his religious head and keep his reputation." In the same page, it is also mentioned, "Selma's reputation would have been ruined and her name would have been blemished by the dirt of lips and t</span>
  <span id="freeText327624521734588643" style="display:none">For me, it's more than just a love story. <br /><br />It is the story of a father who was compelled to marry off his daughter to the Bishop's nephew because his (Farris Effendi) and his daughter - Selma Karamy's reputation would have been ruined had he said no to Bishop. As mentioned in the book, "No man could disobey his religious head and keep his reputation." In the same page, it is also mentioned, "Selma's reputation would have been ruined and her name would have been blemished by the dirt of lips and tongues." Thus, her destiny was sealed liked many women in an oriental society since centuries. <br /><br />It is the story of a nation where religious authorities can manipulate the masses with their concocted innovations in the religion to curry favours from the general public. This is not limited to just one religion or one nation. As mentioned in the book, "The Christian Bishop and the Moslem (Muslim) imam and the Brahman priest become like sea reptiles who clutch their prey with many tentacles and suck their blood with numerous mouths." <br /><br />It is the story of a woman who becomes a commodity. She gets married off not because she was beautiful but because someone was interested in her father's money. Sadly, it's the story of most women in our society where, "the woman is looked upon as a commodity, purchased and delivered from one house to another. In time her beauty fades and she becomes like an old piece of furniture left in a dark corner." That is the sad reality of our society where woman's value is that of furniture. <br /><br />Apparently, Gibran, The Prophet of Lebanon, has disguised all these miseries of our society's sickness in his poetic words and the story looks like a love story where the lovers are separated by the norms of the society.</span>
  <a data-text-id="327624521734588643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1970827614" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1970827614" />
    <a title="Eric" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17825752-eric"><img alt="Eric" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379560052p2/17825752.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1970827614?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric" href="/user/show/17825752-eric">Eric</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1970827614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13609714313859034520">When someone recommended <i>The Broken Wings</i>, I vaguely remembered having read a couple of quotes from <i>Sand and Foam</i> and thinking they were insightful and/or beautiful, so I thought it worth a try. <br/><br/>I realize that this is a book from another time and place, but the magniloquence at times made me want to snicker rather than feel the gravitas of tragedy. Maybe you have to be in a certain frame of mind to appreciate it -- like young and in love and feeling an irresistible urge to write poetry that uses</span>
  <span id="freeText13609714313859034520" style="display:none">When someone recommended <i>The Broken Wings</i>, I vaguely remembered having read a couple of quotes from <i>Sand and Foam</i> and thinking they were insightful and/or beautiful, so I thought it worth a try. <br /><br />I realize that this is a book from another time and place, but the magniloquence at times made me want to snicker rather than feel the gravitas of tragedy. Maybe you have to be in a certain frame of mind to appreciate it -- like young and in love and feeling an irresistible urge to write poetry that uses the word "soul" a lot.<br /><br />The imagery sometimes came in such rapid succession that it was like painting over and over on a wet canvas until there was just mud.<br /><br />In terms of the story, while I appreciate honor and fidelity even in a hard situation, there's a certain relish in fated misery, as in this climactic response when the protagonist says (effectively) to his love, "Maybe we should just run away together": <br /><br /><blockquote>No, no my beloved. Heaven placed in my hand a cup, full of vinegar and gall; I forced myself to drink it in order to know the full bitterness at the bottom until nothing was left save a few drops, which I shall drink patiently. I am not worthy of a new life of love and peace; I am not strong enough for life’s pleasure and sweetness, because a bird with broken wings cannot fly in the spacious sky.</blockquote><br /><br />I was pleased, though, that the book wasn't very long.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13609714313859034520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2346455018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11298416878524743270"><b>The Broken Wings</b> truly depicts the reality of our society where some people still likes to rule over women. Women is nothing for them but a slave. <br/><br/>It's a tragic love story that starts when writer <i>(Jibran)</i> himself fell in love with a girl <i>Selma.</i> <i>Selma's</i> father <i>Faris Effendi</i> was an old friend of <i>Jibran's</i> father and he introduced <i>Selma and Jibran.</i><br/><br/><i>Faris Effendi</i> was compelled to marry his daughter to <i>Bishop's nephew.</i> Bishop was interested in this marriage not because of Salma's beauty and inteligence</span>
  <span id="freeText11298416878524743270" style="display:none"><b>The Broken Wings</b> truly depicts the reality of our society where some people still likes to rule over women. Women is nothing for them but a slave. <br /><br />It's a tragic love story that starts when writer <i>(Jibran)</i> himself fell in love with a girl <i>Selma.</i> <i>Selma's</i> father <i>Faris Effendi</i> was an old friend of <i>Jibran's</i> father and he introduced <i>Selma and Jibran.</i><br /><br /><i>Faris Effendi</i> was compelled to marry his daughter to <i>Bishop's nephew.</i> Bishop was interested in this marriage not because of Salma's beauty and inteligence but for her property.<br /><br />After some months Selma lost her father. <i>Selma and Jibran</i> used to meet each other secretly in a temple and share their love and sorrows. <br /><br />When selma realized that Bishop kept an eye on Selma and Jibran so they ended their meeting.<br /> <br />Her husband always treated her like a slave. After 5 years she gave birth to a boy, unfortunately he died. Selma was unable to bear this pain so she hit herself against the wall. At the end of the day there were two dead bodies.<br />She was buried with her son upon her <i>Father's ditch.</i><br /><br />The end was really heart wrenching!<br /><br />The thing i don't like in this book was too much use of metaphors. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>3.5 stars</b>
</i> ⭐⭐⭐</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tcnN4++1i9/RGiAm2mg1I+N9FcQd1gwmt+I/K0ksVWowua7jcuA+W/VxFGIjMlck9RnKxsv53RFP+YJ1iGMAEw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kAS1OcaqFRoLWhme0UTFZYYMJc5JmHBxAh7TCDF7flIVdNY5W/+gni8xLdooHqdikGj6zJ+3oUb6BW5W8DQrKw==')})
  }

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_38595700').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6466154.Kahlil_Gibran">About Kahlil Gibran</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/6466154.Kahlil_Gibran"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1353732571p3/6466154.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13331640928640881445">Kahlil Gibran (Arabic: <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17888244.________________' title='جبران خليل جبران' rel='nofollow noopener'>جبران خليل جبران</a>
</b>) was a Lebanese-American artist, poet, and writer. <br/>Born in the town of Bsharri in modern-day Lebanon (then part of Ottoman Mount Lebanon), as a young man he emigrated with his family to the United States where he studied art and began his literary career. In the Arab world, Gibran is regarded as a literary and political rebel. His romantic style was at t</span>
  <span id="freeText13331640928640881445" style="display:none">Kahlil Gibran (Arabic: <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17888244.________________" title="جبران خليل جبران" rel="nofollow noopener">جبران خليل جبران</a>
</b>) was a Lebanese-American artist, poet, and writer. <br />Born in the town of Bsharri in modern-day Lebanon (then part of Ottoman Mount Lebanon), as a young man he emigrated with his family to the United States where he studied art and began his literary career. In the Arab world, Gibran is regarded as a literary and political rebel. His romantic style was at the heart of a renaissance in modern Arabic literature, especially prose poetry, breaking away from the classical school. In Lebanon, he is still celebrated as a literary hero. <br />He is chiefly known in the English-speaking world for his 1923 book <i>The Prophet</i>, an early example of inspirational fiction including a series of philosophical essays written in poetic English prose. The book sold well despite a cool critical reception, gaining popularity in the 1930s and again especially in the 1960s counterculture. <br />Gibran is the third best-selling poet of all time, behind Shakespeare and Lao-Tzu.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13331640928640881445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
